البينتين قامتا على مطلق الملك ولم يتعرضا لجهة الملك فكان التقدم والتأخر سواء ولهما أن البينة مع التاريخ متضمنة معنى الدفع فإن الملك إذا ثبت لشخص في وقت فثبوته لغيره بعده لا يكون إلا بالتلقي من جهته وبينة ذي اليد على الدفع مقبولة وعلى هذا الخلاف لو كانت الدار في أيديهما والمعنى ما بينا. قيد بسبق تاريخ ذي اليد لأنه لو لم يكن لهما تاريخ أو استوى تاريخهما أو أرخت إحداهما فقط كان الخارج أولى، وكذا لو كانت في أيديهما فإنها تقدم المؤقتة على غيرها (قلت الخ) أقول : إذا عرف الشهود أن البائع وكيل فالظاهر أنهم يقولون باعها بالوكالة عمن يملكها على أنك علمت مما نقلناه آنفاً أن خصوص وهو يملكها غير لازم.
Book of Claims, Chapter on the Claim of Two Men: Their dates or the precedence of one's date, contrary to when the property belongs to one person where the earlier is given priority; thus the commentator mentioned following al-Kafi, and it is a mistake, rather the earlier is given priority here as well. And what is meant by his saying as in al-Hidayah: 'they mentioned a date of equality in it' i.e., one date. Therefore it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'If the date of one is earlier, he is given priority according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the last opinion of Abu Yusuf, and it is the opinion of Muhammad in the narration of Abu Hafs. And according to the first opinion of Abu Yusuf, it is judged between them half and half, because they both establish ownership for their sellers, so it is as if the two sellers appeared and claimed absolute ownership for themselves, and the ruling in the claim of absolute ownership is that, so here as well.' And in Khazanat al-Akmal: 'It is mentioned in the book: if they dated two times, the owner of the first time is given priority.' And the commentator is surprised that he made it a case of absolute ownership claim and forgot what he said in the book recently: 'If the two outsiders prove with ownership and date, the earlier is more entitled.' And if the author said 'they mentioned a date or one of them only' it would be better, so the owner of the date is not preferred over the other because the dating of one does not indicate the precedence of ownership, as it is possible that the other is earlier, contrary to when the seller is one, because they agree that ownership is only received from his side, so if one proves a date, it is judged by it until it becomes clear that he was preceded in purchase by another. Then know that testimony about purchase is not accepted until they testify that he bought it from so-and-so and he... For there is no difference in all other rulings between that one being the holder or other. So since the rulings are unified, there is no benefit in lengthening. Consider his saying: 'It is a mistake etc.' al-Ramli said: 'Rather the mistake is from him, not from the commentator and al-Kafi, because the issue has a difference of narration.' Then Jami' al-Fusulayn transmitted what we presented, investigating the same in the commentary of the text: 'If they date, the earlier is given priority.' So refer to it. The conclusion is that what the commentator al-Zayla'i followed agrees with what is in al-Hidayah, and it is what the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn preferred. His saying: 'Rather the earlier is given priority here as well' i.e., when the transferor is multiple as when it is single. His saying: 'And the surprise at the commentator' al-Ramli said: 'There is no surprise from him, rather the surprise is from you, because the ownership of the sellers is ownership without date, as known from his saying: it is as if they appeared and proved absolute ownership without date. And the issue of the book is about the proof of the two outsiders on absolute ownership and date, and in it the earlier is more entitled, so between the two issues there is a difference; so what surprise is from the commentator? Rather the surprise is from you.' Consider his saying: 'Then know that testimony about purchase etc.' He said in Nur al-Ayn at the end of the sixth chapter, alluding to al-Mabsut: 'Testimony about purchase from an absentee is not accepted except by testifying with one of three: either by the ownership of his seller by saying he sold while owning it, or by the ownership of his buyer by saying it is for the buyer he bought it from so-and-so, or by his possession by saying he bought it from him and took possession.' And in it, alluding to the fatwas of al-Qadi Zahir: 'If someone claimed inheritance from his father and another claimed purchase from the deceased, and their witnesses testified that the deceased sold it to him and did not say that he sold it while owning it, they said: if the house was in the hand of the claimant of purchase or the claimant of inheritance, the testimony is valid because it is about mere sale; it is only not accepted if the house is not in the hand of the buyer or heir. But if it was, then the testimony of sale is like testimony of sale and ownership.' On purchase from one, the earlier is more entitled; on purchase from another and they mentioned a date, they are equal. And if they prove ownership, no, the outsider proves ownership with a date and the date of the holder is earlier, or they prove by offspring or a recurring cause, or the outsider proves ownership and the holder proves purchase from him, then the holder is more entitled. And if each proves that so-and-so owns it, as in Khazanat al-Akmal. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'Testimony about purchase from a specific person is not accepted until they testify that he sold it to him while on that day he owned it, or they testify that it is for this claimant, he bought it from so-and-so for such and such, paid the price, and he handed it over to him, because a person may sell what he does not own, as it is possible he is an agent or a transgressor, so the buyer does not deserve ownership by that. Therefore it is necessary to mention the ownership of the seller or what indicates it.' I say: If the seller is an agent, how can they testify that he sold it while owning it? Let it be considered. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: 'If the sold item is in the hand of the seller, it is accepted without mentioning the seller's ownership. If it is in the hand of another and the claimant claims it for himself, if the claimant and his witnesses mention that the seller owns it, or they said he handed it over to him and he said he handed it over to me, or he said I took possession and they said he took possession, or he said it is mine I bought it from him and it is mine, it is accepted. If they testify about the sale and payment but do not mention possession or delivery or the seller's ownership or the buyer's ownership, the claim and testimony are not accepted. If they testify about the hand of the seller without ownership, they differed.' And if they are equal in the issue of the book, it is judged between them half and half, then each is given the choice: if he wishes, he takes half of the slave for half the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. And the author indicated that if one claimed purchase from a man who owns it, and the other claimed gift from another and possession from him while he owns it, then it is between them. Hence it is said in al-Hidayah: 'If one claimed purchase from a man, another claimed gift and possession from another, the third inheritance from his father, and the other charity and possession from another, it is judged between them in fourths, because they receive ownership from their sellers, so they are made as if they appeared and established testimony on absolute ownership.' His saying: 'If the outsider proves ownership with a date and the date of the holder is earlier, or they prove by offspring or ownership that does not recur, or the outsider proves ownership and the holder proves purchase from him, then the holder is more entitled' is an explanation of three issues in which the holder's testimony prevails over the outsider's: First: they both prove ownership with a date and the holder's date is earlier, and this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and there is a narration from Muhammad and from him its non-acceptance, he returned to it because the two testimonies stand on absolute ownership and did not address the source of ownership, so precedence and lateness are equal. And according to them, the testimony with date includes the meaning of defense, because if ownership is established for a person at a time, its establishment for another after that can only be by receiving from his side, and the holder's testimony on defense is accepted. And on this difference, if the house was in both their hands, the meaning is as we explained. It is conditioned by the precedence of the holder's date because if they had no date, or their dates were equal, or only one of them was dated, the outsider is given priority. Likewise if it was in both their hands, then the dated one is preferred over the other. (I say etc.) I say: If the witnesses know that the seller is an agent, apparently they say he sold it by proxy from the one who owns it, as you know from what we transmitted earlier that the specific 'and he owns it' is not necessary.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and commentary on the ruling when two claimants each produce a proof with a date, but they claim from different transferors (e.g., each bought from a different person). The initial position of the commentator (al-Zayla'i) following al-Kafi is that when the transferors are multiple, the earlier date is not given priority, unlike when there is one transferor. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq corrects this, stating it is a mistake and that the earlier date should be given priority here as well. He cites al-Hidayah and Ghayat al-Bayan, which present the views of the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and the later opinion of Abu Yusuf, as well as Muhammad in one narration, favor the earlier date. The first opinion of Abu Yusuf (that they split half and half) is based on the reasoning that both claimants establish ownership for their respective sellers, making it as if both sellers claimed absolute ownership, which would result in equal division. The author then quotes from Khazanat al-Akmal that if both date, the earlier date is preferred. He criticizes the commentator for categorizing this as a case of absolute ownership, forgetting that in the book it is stated that if outsiders prove ownership and date, the earlier is more entitled. The discussion continues with al-Ramli defending the commentator, noting that the issue has differing narrations. The passage then shifts to the conditions for accepting testimony on purchase: it is not accepted unless the witnesses mention the seller's ownership, the buyer's ownership, or possession. This is derived from Nur al-Ayn and al-Mabsut. Further, if the holder (dhu al-yad) has a dated proof that is earlier, or if both prove by offspring or a recurring cause, or if the outsider proves ownership and the holder proves purchase from him, the holder is more entitled. The text then addresses the case when both have equal proofs: they split half, and each may choose to take half or leave. Finally, an example from al-Hidayah illustrates multiple claimants with different causes (purchase, gift, inheritance, charity) leading to equal shares in fourths. The commentary emphasizes that the Hanafi school gives priority to the earlier date even when transferors differ, and that testimony on purchase must include evidence of the seller's ownership or equivalent to prevent fraud.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Proof or evidence, typically testimony of witnesses or documentary evidence establishing a claim in court.
التاريخ (al-tarikh): The date recorded in the proof of purchase or ownership, used to determine precedence.
ذو اليد (dhu al-yad): The person who currently possesses the property in dispute, the holder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two claimants each produce a proof of purchase with a date, but they claim to have purchased from different owners, what is the Hanafi ruling according to al-Hidayah?
A) The property is divided equally between them.
B) The one with the earlier date is given priority.
C) The property is awarded to the person currently in possession.
D) The case is dismissed due to conflicting proof.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when two claimants produce dated proofs of purchase from different sellers, the earlier date determines entitlement, as upheld by Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon opinion.

Claim of Paternity for Child of a Purchased Slave Girl
Stating the ruling on paternity claim for child of purchased slave girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on claiming paternity when a purchased slave girl gives birth, identifying the conditions for acceptance of the seller's and buyer's claims based on the time of birth.

Core Idea
Paternity claim on a purchased slave girl's child depends on timing: within six months from sale favors the seller; beyond six months, only if buyer confirms.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a clear set of rulings for a specific scenario: a purchased slave girl gives birth, and either the seller or the buyer claims paternity. The Hanafi school uses the minimum pregnancy period (six months) as a decisive factor. Understanding these rules is important for cases involving sale of slaves with potential paternity claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key variables
Note the two parties: seller and buyer. The key variable is the time of birth relative to the sale: within six months (the minimum pregnancy period) or after more than six months.
Six months is the minimum pregnancy duration in Hanafi law.
2
Seller's claim within six months
If the birth occurs within six months from the sale, the seller's claim is accepted: the child is his son, the slave becomes his umm walad, the sale is annulled (فسخ), and the price is returned.
The sale is rescinded because the child and slave belong to the seller.
3
Buyer's claim within six months
The buyer's claim of paternity is also accepted. If the buyer claims the child, the child becomes his son and the slave his umm walad; the sale remains valid as he already owns the mother.
The text says 'وإن ادعاه المشتري أو بعده' – implying the buyer's claim is accepted whether made before or after the birth.
4
Effect of death or emancipation
If the mother dies, the claim is still effective – the child remains with the claimant. But if the child dies, the claim becomes moot. Emancipation (عتق) of either the mother or child is treated like death – the claim is no longer applicable.
The text: 'بخلاف موت الولد وعتقهما كموتهما' – the consequence of child's death unlike mother's death; freeing them both is like their death.
5
Birth after six months
If the birth occurs after six months from the sale, the seller's claim is rejected (ردت دعوة البائع) unless the buyer confirms (يصدقه المشتري) the seller's paternity.
Because the minimum pregnancy from the seller's ownership is not met, so the child is presumed to be from another father unless the buyer testifies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولدت مبيعة لأقل مدة الحمل مذ بيعت فادعاه البائع فهو ابنه وهي أم ولده ويفسخ ويرد الثمن وإن ادعاه المشتري أو بعده، وكذا إن ماتت الأم بخلاف موت الولد وعتقهما كموتهما، وإن ولدت لأكثر من ستة أشهر ردت دعوة البائع إلا أن يصدقه المشتري. ومن ادعى نسب أحد التوأمين معه
If a purchased [slave girl] gives birth for less than the minimum period of pregnancy from the time she was sold, and the seller claims him (the child), then he is his son and she is his umm walad, and the sale is rescinded and the price is returned. And if the buyer claims him, [it is accepted] before or after? And similarly if the mother dies, unlike if the child dies, and their emancipation is like their death. And if she gives birth after more than six months, the seller's claim is rejected unless the buyer confirms him. And whoever claims paternity of one of the twins with him...
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Claims of Paternity (Bāb Da'wā al-Nasab) provides concise rulings. When a purchased slave girl gives birth, the seller can claim paternity if the birth occurs within the minimum possible period of pregnancy (six months) from the date of sale. If accepted, the child becomes his son, the slave girl becomes his umm walad, the sale is annulled, and the price is returned. If the buyer claims paternity, it is also accepted. Different rules apply if the mother dies vs. the child dies; emancipation of either is treated like death. If the birth occurs after six months from sale, the seller's claim is rejected unless the buyer attests to it. The passage ends with an incomplete sentence about claim of twin.

Key Terms
دعوى النسب (da'wa al-nasab): Legal claim of paternity of a child.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death.
مدة الحمل (muddat al-haml): The minimum period of pregnancy, which is six months in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a purchased slave girl gives birth seven months after the sale, what is the ruling on the seller's claim of paternity?
A) It is accepted because the birth is after six months
B) It is rejected unless the buyer confirms
C) It is rejected unconditionally
D) The child is considered free

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the paternity claim of a seller on a purchased slave girl's child is accepted only if the birth occurs within six months of the sale; otherwise, the claim is rejected unless the buyer confirms it.

Interpretation of 'Kadha' and Fractions in Iqrar
شرح قاعدة تفسير الأعداد المبهمة في الإقرار

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of the ambiguous term 'kadha' in iqrar and apply it to determine the amount owed when a fraction is mentioned.

Core Idea
كذا = 3 when singular, 11 when repeated; fractions add by custom multiples.

In this passage, al-Bahr al-Raiq explains how Hanafi jurists interpret ambiguous numerical expressions in confessions. The term 'kadha' is a placeholder that must be clarified by customary usage. You will learn the precise numbers associated with different patterns of 'kadha' and the effect of fractions like 'thulth' and 'rub'' on the total.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase
Look at the phrase the confessor used, e.g., 'kadha dirhaman' or 'kadha kadha dirhaman'.
The word 'kadha' is a mubham (ambiguous word) that needs interpretation.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule for 'kadha'
If 'kadha' appears once, it means 3 (the minimum of a plural). If repeated as 'kadha kadha', it means 11. If connected with 'waw', e.g., 'kadha wa kadha', it means 21.
The numbers are based on linguistic conventions: 'kadha' = 3, 'kadha kadha' = 3+3+5=11, 'kadha wa kadha' = 11+10=21.
3
Handle fractions with and without waw
If the confessor says 'thulth' with waw (e.g., 'thulth wa...'), it adds 100 dirhams. Without waw, it means 11. Similarly, 'rubʻ' with waw adds 1000, 'khums' adds 10,000, etc.
The pattern is: fraction + 'waw' signals addition of a customary number (100, 1000, etc.).
4
Determine the final amount
Combine the base number from 'kadha' with any additions from fractions to get the total amount owed.
Customary weight (وزن معتاد) is considered in each time and place.

Book of Confession. Dirham: 'such-and-such dirham', 'dirham such-and-such such-and-such eleven such-and-such and such-and-such twenty-one', and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] a nisab and great wealth, three nisabs from whatever property he interprets it, and dirhams or little dirhams or something of dirhams or from three dirhams, and many dirhams, or many garments, or many functions, or many dinars, or most dirhams, so ten; and multiplied dirhams six, and multiplied multiples or its opposite eighteen, and valuable or precious or noble or great property, or neither little nor much: two hundred; 'such-and-such dirham': 'such-and-such such-and-such' is eleven, 'such-and-such and such-and-such' is twenty-one; and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand, and if 'a fifth' it adds ten thousand, and if 'a sixth' it adds one hundred thousand, and if 'a seventh' it adds one million; and every number conjuncted with waw is added according to custom ad infinitum; and if 'a third' without waw he owes eleven; and if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and dinar' he owes eleven equally, contrary to if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and such-and-such such-and-such dinar' he owes from each one eleven; and the consideration is the customary weight in every time or place; and 'al-naif' is unknown, one refers to him; and 'al-bad'ah' is for three; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt, unless he interprets it as trust connectedly; and 'he lent me such-and-such' he owes it, but 'I borrowed' no; and 'I have no right from him' is a discharge from debt and trust; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] trust; and 'with me a borrowed thousand dirhams' is a loan; 'he has from me such-and-such deposit' or 'deposit' is a debt; it is absolute; and the principle is that if one of the two words is for trust and the other for debt:
Al-Khaniyyah: He has upon me a garment or a slave – it is valid and he is adjudged to pay the average value according to Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: the statement is his as to value. In Hashiyat al-Hamawi 'ala al-Ashbah from al-Multaqat: If he says 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for a guarantee of the value of the confessed item and his statement is accepted. Bishr said: the sheep is obligatory. End. The shaykh of our shaykhs al-Saihani said: it is possible that what is in al-Ashbah is according to the saying of the Imam. End. Then I saw it in al-Tatarkhaniyyah where he said: In al-Hawi: he said to so-and-so 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Hanifa said: his confession is not valid. Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for the guarantee. Bishr said: According to Abu Hanifa, he owes the sheep but not the house because it is not suitable as a debt; he owes it in dower, and the sheep is suitable. Bishr said: We take by Abu Hanifa's saying. And if he said 'upon me a Herawi garment', his statement is accepted as to the Herawi garment and he is not required to pay an average Herawi garment.
Dirhams: and the word 'multiples'.
His saying: 'And multiplied multiples or its opposite is eighteen' i.e. if he said 'dirhams multiplied multiples' because the plural minimum is three, so it becomes nine, and the double of nine is eighteen. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Iqrar: if he said 'I have upon him multiplied dirhams' he owes six dirhams. And if he said 'multiples as multiples' or said 'multiplied' it is eighteen. In al-Sirajiyyah: if he said 'I have multiples multiplied' he owes twenty-four, because by his saying 'dirhams' he owes three, by his saying 'multiples' nine, and by his saying 'multiplied' twelve, so the total is what we said. His saying: 'and if a fifth it adds ten thousand': some virtuous ones said: this is reported by al-Ayni with the wording 'it should be' but it is a clear error because the ten thousand combine with the thousand without waw, so it is said dirhams.

Commentary
هذا المقطع من البحر الرائق يشرح أحكام الإقرار بالأعداد المبهمة والعبارات التي قد تدل على الأمانة أو الدين. يبدأ بذكر ألفاظ مبهمة مثل 'كذا درهماً' وكيفية تفسيرها. مثلاً، 'كذا درهماً' تعني أحد عشر درهماً، و'كذا وكذا' تعني أحد وعشرين. ثم يبين حكم الكسور: إذا قال 'ثلث' بالواو (أي ثلث و...) يضاف مائة، وإذا قال 'ربع' يضاف ألف، وهكذا. ثم ينتقل إلى عبارات مثل 'عندي معي' التي تعتبر إقراراً بالدين ما لم يفسرها بالأمانة في نفس المجلس. ثم يذكر مسألة 'له علي ثوب أو عبد' وفيها خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد وبشر. وأخيراً يشرح لفظ 'أضعاف مضاعفة' ويذكر اختلاف الأئمة في تفسيرها: بعضهم يوجب ثمانية عشر، وبعضهم أربعة وعشرين. النص يعتمد على العرف والتفسير المتصل في تحديد المبلغ المقر به.

Key Terms
كذا (kadhā): لفظ مبهم للعدد يُفسر في الإقرار بثلاثة عند الإضافة وبأحد عشر عند التكرار.

Trust and Debt Phrases in Iqrar
شرح حكم الألفاظ الدالة على الأمانة والدين

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between phrases that imply a confession of debt and those implying trust, and apply the rule that a connected interpretation can change the legal effect.

Core Idea
عندي/معي = debt unless connectedly interpreted as trust.

This passage clarifies how phrases like 'indī' and 'ma'ī' are interpreted in confessions. The default assumption is that they indicate a debt, but if the confessor immediately adds that it is an amanah (trust), it becomes a trust. You will also learn about phrases like 'aqraḍanī' (he lent me), 'istaqraḍtu' (I borrowed), and the effect of 'lā ḥaqq lī' (I have no right).

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial phrase
Phrases like 'علي' (upon me), 'قبلي' (with me), 'عندي' (with me), 'معي' (with me) are generally considered confessions of debt.
The default is that these words imply a financial obligation.
2
Check for connected interpretation
If the confessor immediately follows the phrase with an interpretation that it is an amanah (trust), without a break, then it is treated as a trust, not a debt.
The interpretation must be متصل (connected) to be effective.
3
Distinguish between lending and borrowing
If the confessor says 'أقرضني' (he lent me), it is a confession of debt. If he says 'استقرضت' (I borrowed), it is not a confession unless confirmed.
The active voice 'aqraḍanī' imposes a liability; 'istaqraḍtu' is a claim that needs proof.
4
Apply the principle of mixed phrases
When one word indicates trust and another indicates debt (e.g., 'وديعة' and 'دين'), the phrase is interpreted as debt unless there is a connected interpretation.
The original is that one of the two words is for trust, the other for debt, but the default is debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإقرار
٤٢٥
درهم
كذا درهماً درهم كذا كذا أحد عشر كذا وكذا أحد وعشرون ولو ثلث بالواو يزاد مائة ولو ربع زيد ألف علي أو قبلي إقرار بدين عندي معي في بيتي في صندوقي في كيسي نصاب وأموال عظام ثلاثة نصب من أي مال فسره به ودارهم ) أو دريهمات أو شيء من الدراهم أو من دراهم ثلاثة) ودراهم كثيرة) أو ثياب كثيرة أو وظائف كثيرة أو دنانير كثيرة أو أكثر الدراهم ف(عشرة) ودراهم مضاعفة ستة وأضعاف مضاعفة أو عكسه ثمانية عشر ومال نفيس أو خطير أو كريم أو جليل أو لا قليل ولا كثير مائتان كذا درهما . كذا كذا أحد عشر كذا وكذا أحد وعشرون ولو ثلث بالواو يزاد مائة ولو ربع زيد ألف ولو خمس زيد عشرة آلاف، ولو سدس يزاد مائة ألف، ولو سبع يزاد ألف ألف، وكل ما زاد عدداً معطوفاً بالواو زيد عليه ما جرت العادة به إلى ما لا يتناهى، ولو ثلث بلا واو لزمه أحد عشر، ولو قال كذا كذا درهماً وديناراً فعليه أحد عشر بالسوية بخلاف ما إذا قال كذا كذا درهماً وكذا كذا ديناراً لزمه من كل واحد أحد عشر والمعتبر الوزن المعتاد في كل زمان أو مكان، والنيف مجهول يرجع إليه فيه والبضعة للثلاثة على وقبلي إقرار بالدين) إلا إذا فسره بالأمانة متصلاً وأقرضني كذا لزمه واستقرضت لا وليس لي قبله حق إبراء عن الدين والأمانة (عندي معي في بيتي في صندوقي في كيسي أمانة وعندي عارية ألف درهم قرض له قبلي - كذا وديعة أو وديعة دين فهو دين ،مطلق، والأصل أن أحد اللفظين إذا كان للأمانة والآخر للدين
دین
الخانية : له علي ثوب أو عبد صح ويقضى بقيمة وسط عند أبي يوسف وقال محمد: القول له في القيمة. وفي حاشية الحموي على الأشباه عن الملتقط : إذا قال علي دار أو شاة قال أبو يوسف : يلزمه الضمان بقيمة المقر به والقول قوله. وقال بشر : تجب الشاة .اهـ. قال شيخ مشايخنا السائحاني : يمكن
:
أن يكون ما في الأشباه على قول الإمام .اهـ. ثم رأيته في التتارخانية حيث قال: وفي الحاوي قال لفلان علي دار أو شاة قال أبو حنيفة : لا يصح إقراره. وقال أبو يوسف لزمه الضمان . وقال بشر : ينبغي أن عند أبي حنيفة لزمه الشاة دون الدار لأنها لا تصلح ديناً لزمه في الصداق والشاة تصلح قال بشر : وبقول أبي حنيفة نأخذ ولو قال علي ثوب هروي فالقول قوله في الثوب الهروي ولا يلزمه
ثوب هروي وسط .
دارهم
وأضعاف لفظه
قوله : (وأضعاف مضاعفة أو عكسه ثمانية عشر أي لو قال دراهم أضعاف مضاعفة لأن جمع وأقله ثلاثة فتصير تسعة وضعف التسعة ثمانية عشر. وفي التتارخانية ما نصه : ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في شرح كتاب الإقرار إذا قال لفلان علي دراهم مضاعفة فعليه ستة دراهم. ولو قال مضاعفة أضعافاً أو قال مضاعفة فهي ثمانية عشر. وفي السراجية: لو قال له أضعاف مضاعفة لزمته أربعة وعشرون لأن بقوله دراهم لزمه ثلاثة، وبقوله أضعافاً تسعة، وبقوله مضاعفة اثني عشر فجملته ما قلنا قوله: (ولو خمس زيد عشرة ألاف) قال بعض الفضلاء : هذا حكاه العيني بلفظ ينبغي لكنه غلط ظاهر لأن العشرة الآلاف تتركب مع الألف بلا واو فيقال
دراهم
Book of Confession. Dirham: 'such-and-such dirham', 'dirham such-and-such such-and-such eleven such-and-such and such-and-such twenty-one', and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] a nisab and great wealth, three nisabs from whatever property he interprets it, and dirhams or little dirhams or something of dirhams or from three dirhams, and many dirhams, or many garments, or many functions, or many dinars, or most dirhams, so ten; and multiplied dirhams six, and multiplied multiples or its opposite eighteen, and valuable or precious or noble or great property, or neither little nor much: two hundred; 'such-and-such dirham': 'such-and-such such-and-such' is eleven, 'such-and-such and such-and-such' is twenty-one; and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand, and if 'a fifth' it adds ten thousand, and if 'a sixth' it adds one hundred thousand, and if 'a seventh' it adds one million; and every number conjuncted with waw is added according to custom ad infinitum; and if 'a third' without waw he owes eleven; and if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and dinar' he owes eleven equally, contrary to if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and such-and-such such-and-such dinar' he owes from each one eleven; and the consideration is the customary weight in every time or place; and 'al-naif' is unknown, one refers to him; and 'al-bad'ah' is for three; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt, unless he interprets it as trust connectedly; and 'he lent me such-and-such' he owes it, but 'I borrowed' no; and 'I have no right from him' is a discharge from debt and trust; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] trust; and 'with me a borrowed thousand dirhams' is a loan; 'he has from me such-and-such deposit' or 'deposit' is a debt; it is absolute; and the principle is that if one of the two words is for trust and the other for debt:
Al-Khaniyyah: He has upon me a garment or a slave – it is valid and he is adjudged to pay the average value according to Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: the statement is his as to value. In Hashiyat al-Hamawi 'ala al-Ashbah from al-Multaqat: If he says 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for a guarantee of the value of the confessed item and his statement is accepted. Bishr said: the sheep is obligatory. End. The shaykh of our shaykhs al-Saihani said: it is possible that what is in al-Ashbah is according to the saying of the Imam. End. Then I saw it in al-Tatarkhaniyyah where he said: In al-Hawi: he said to so-and-so 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Hanifa said: his confession is not valid. Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for the guarantee. Bishr said: According to Abu Hanifa, he owes the sheep but not the house because it is not suitable as a debt; he owes it in dower, and the sheep is suitable. Bishr said: We take by Abu Hanifa's saying. And if he said 'upon me a Herawi garment', his statement is accepted as to the Herawi garment and he is not required to pay an average Herawi garment.
Dirhams: and the word 'multiples'.
His saying: 'And multiplied multiples or its opposite is eighteen' i.e. if he said 'dirhams multiplied multiples' because the plural minimum is three, so it becomes nine, and the double of nine is eighteen. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Iqrar: if he said 'I have upon him multiplied dirhams' he owes six dirhams. And if he said 'multiples as multiples' or said 'multiplied' it is eighteen. In al-Sirajiyyah: if he said 'I have multiples multiplied' he owes twenty-four, because by his saying 'dirhams' he owes three, by his saying 'multiples' nine, and by his saying 'multiplied' twelve, so the total is what we said. His saying: 'and if a fifth it adds ten thousand': some virtuous ones said: this is reported by al-Ayni with the wording 'it should be' but it is a clear error because the ten thousand combine with the thousand without waw, so it is said dirhams.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
هذا المقطع من البحر الرائق يشرح أحكام الإقرار بالأعداد المبهمة والعبارات التي قد تدل على الأمانة أو الدين. يبدأ بذكر ألفاظ مبهمة مثل 'كذا درهماً' وكيفية تفسيرها. مثلاً، 'كذا درهماً' تعني أحد عشر درهماً، و'كذا وكذا' تعني أحد وعشرين. ثم يبين حكم الكسور: إذا قال 'ثلث' بالواو (أي ثلث و...) يضاف مائة، وإذا قال 'ربع' يضاف ألف، وهكذا. ثم ينتقل إلى عبارات مثل 'عندي معي' التي تعتبر إقراراً بالدين ما لم يفسرها بالأمانة في نفس المجلس. ثم يذكر مسألة 'له علي ثوب أو عبد' وفيها خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد وبشر. وأخيراً يشرح لفظ 'أضعاف مضاعفة' ويذكر اختلاف الأئمة في تفسيرها: بعضهم يوجب ثمانية عشر، وبعضهم أربعة وعشرين. النص يعتمد على العرف والتفسير المتصل في تحديد المبلغ المقر به.

Key Terms
عندي (indī): لفظ يُفسر إقراراً بالدين ما لم يفسره بالأمانة متصلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a confession of debt according to the Hanafi school?
A) استقرضت
B) عندي وديعة
C) ليس لي قبله حق
D) أقرضني

Key Takeaway
Phrases like 'indī' default as debt; only a connected interpretation as trust changes the status.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Confession of Specific Items and Multiples
بيان حكم الإقرار بالعين وحساب الأضعاف المضاعفة

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on confessing a specific item (e.g., garment, slave, house) and calculate the amount owed for 'ad'āf mudā'afah' (multiplied multiples).

Core Idea
Confession of a specific item like a house is invalid; 'ad'āf mudā'afah' = 18 or 24 depending on the phrasing.

This passage covers two distinct but important sub-topics in iqrar: first, the ruling when someone confesses to a specific item that may or may not be suitable as a debt, and second, the interpretation of the phrase 'ad'āf mudā'afah' (multiplied multiples). You will learn the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Bishr regarding the first issue, and the calculation methods for the second.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specificity of the confessed item
If the confessor says 'له علي ثوب أو عبد' (a garment or a slave), the item may be suitable as a debt. If he says 'دار أو شاة' (a house or a sheep), evaluate suitability.
A house is immovable and not typically a debt; a sheep is movable and can be a debt.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's distinction
Abu Hanifa holds that an item that cannot be a debt (like a house) renders the confession invalid. For items that can be a debt (like a sheep), it is valid.
Bishr adopts this view.
3
Contrast with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf says the confessor must pay the value of the item. Muhammad says the confessor's word on the value is accepted.
These are intra-Hanafi differences.
4
Calculate 'ad'āf mudā'afah'
If someone says 'دراهم مضاعفة' he owes 6 dirhams; 'أضعاف مضاعفة' = 18; 'أضعاف مضاعفة' with 'أضعافاً' = 18; 'أضعاف مضاعفة' in Sirajiyyah = 24.
The calculation depends on the count of 'ad'āf' (multiples) and the number of times multiplication is applied.

دراهم
Book of Confession. Dirham: 'such-and-such dirham', 'dirham such-and-such such-and-such eleven such-and-such and such-and-such twenty-one', and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] a nisab and great wealth, three nisabs from whatever property he interprets it, and dirhams or little dirhams or something of dirhams or from three dirhams, and many dirhams, or many garments, or many functions, or many dinars, or most dirhams, so ten; and multiplied dirhams six, and multiplied multiples or its opposite eighteen, and valuable or precious or noble or great property, or neither little nor much: two hundred; 'such-and-such dirham': 'such-and-such such-and-such' is eleven, 'such-and-such and such-and-such' is twenty-one; and if 'a third' with waw it adds one hundred, and if 'a quarter' it adds one thousand, and if 'a fifth' it adds ten thousand, and if 'a sixth' it adds one hundred thousand, and if 'a seventh' it adds one million; and every number conjuncted with waw is added according to custom ad infinitum; and if 'a third' without waw he owes eleven; and if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and dinar' he owes eleven equally, contrary to if he says 'such-and-such such-and-such dirham and such-and-such such-and-such dinar' he owes from each one eleven; and the consideration is the customary weight in every time or place; and 'al-naif' is unknown, one refers to him; and 'al-bad'ah' is for three; 'upon me' or 'with me' is a confession of debt, unless he interprets it as trust connectedly; and 'he lent me such-and-such' he owes it, but 'I borrowed' no; and 'I have no right from him' is a discharge from debt and trust; 'with me', 'with me', 'in my house', 'in my box', 'in my bag' [is] trust; and 'with me a borrowed thousand dirhams' is a loan; 'he has from me such-and-such deposit' or 'deposit' is a debt; it is absolute; and the principle is that if one of the two words is for trust and the other for debt:
Al-Khaniyyah: He has upon me a garment or a slave – it is valid and he is adjudged to pay the average value according to Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: the statement is his as to value. In Hashiyat al-Hamawi 'ala al-Ashbah from al-Multaqat: If he says 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for a guarantee of the value of the confessed item and his statement is accepted. Bishr said: the sheep is obligatory. End. The shaykh of our shaykhs al-Saihani said: it is possible that what is in al-Ashbah is according to the saying of the Imam. End. Then I saw it in al-Tatarkhaniyyah where he said: In al-Hawi: he said to so-and-so 'upon me a house or a sheep', Abu Hanifa said: his confession is not valid. Abu Yusuf said: he is liable for the guarantee. Bishr said: According to Abu Hanifa, he owes the sheep but not the house because it is not suitable as a debt; he owes it in dower, and the sheep is suitable. Bishr said: We take by Abu Hanifa's saying. And if he said 'upon me a Herawi garment', his statement is accepted as to the Herawi garment and he is not required to pay an average Herawi garment.
Dirhams: and the word 'multiples'.
His saying: 'And multiplied multiples or its opposite is eighteen' i.e. if he said 'dirhams multiplied multiples' because the plural minimum is three, so it becomes nine, and the double of nine is eighteen. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Iqrar: if he said 'I have upon him multiplied dirhams' he owes six dirhams. And if he said 'multiples as multiples' or said 'multiplied' it is eighteen. In al-Sirajiyyah: if he said 'I have multiples multiplied' he owes twenty-four, because by his saying 'dirhams' he owes three, by his saying 'multiples' nine, and by his saying 'multiplied' twelve, so the total is what we said. His saying: 'and if a fifth it adds ten thousand': some virtuous ones said: this is reported by al-Ayni with the wording 'it should be' but it is a clear error because the ten thousand combine with the thousand without waw, so it is said dirhams.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
هذا المقطع من البحر الرائق يشرح أحكام الإقرار بالأعداد المبهمة والعبارات التي قد تدل على الأمانة أو الدين. يبدأ بذكر ألفاظ مبهمة مثل 'كذا درهماً' وكيفية تفسيرها. مثلاً، 'كذا درهماً' تعني أحد عشر درهماً، و'كذا وكذا' تعني أحد وعشرين. ثم يبين حكم الكسور: إذا قال 'ثلث' بالواو (أي ثلث و...) يضاف مائة، وإذا قال 'ربع' يضاف ألف، وهكذا. ثم ينتقل إلى عبارات مثل 'عندي معي' التي تعتبر إقراراً بالدين ما لم يفسرها بالأمانة في نفس المجلس. ثم يذكر مسألة 'له علي ثوب أو عبد' وفيها خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد وبشر. وأخيراً يشرح لفظ 'أضعاف مضاعفة' ويذكر اختلاف الأئمة في تفسيرها: بعضهم يوجب ثمانية عشر، وبعضهم أربعة وعشرين. النص يعتمد على العرف والتفسير المتصل في تحديد المبلغ المقر به.

Key Terms
أضعاف مضاعفة (aḍ'āf muḍā'afah): تعبير في الإقرار يُفسر بثمانية عشر عند البعض وأربعة وعشرين عند آخرين بحسب الجمع والتضعيف.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Bishr's adoption of Abu Hanifa, if someone says 'علي دار أو شاة', what is the ruling?
A) He owes both the house and the sheep
B) He owes the value of the house
C) He owes the sheep only
D) He owes nothing

Key Takeaway
Confession of a specific item is only valid if the item can be a debt, and 'ad'āf mudā'afah' is calculated as 18 or 24 dirhams depending on the interpretation.

Verbal Responses in Confession: What Counts and What Doesn't
Listing of verbal responses that are and are not confessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify verbal responses to a debt claim as confession or non-confession according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Not every answer is a confession; the response must acknowledge the debt, not merely comment on it.

When someone claims you owe them money, your reply matters deeply in Islamic law. Some responses automatically count as an admission of the debt, while others are neutral or even a denial. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on which verbal responses are considered confessions and which are not, so you can correctly identify when a debt is established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Start with the trigger: the claimant says 'You owe me X' or similar. This is the context for the response.
2
Examine the response
Look at the exact words the alleged debtor uses. The Hanafi school categorizes these into responses that imply acknowledgment (confession) and those that do not.
Responses like 'weigh it' or 'give me time' imply the debt exists. Responses like 'I did not take possession unjustly' or 'release me' do not.
3
Check for jest or special context
If both parties agree the statement was made in jest, it is not a confession. Also, certain responses are not confessions even if they sound like it, like 'I paid your brother by your command' (requires proof).
4
Apply the rule
If the response indicates an intention to pay, measure, transfer, or refers to the debt as owed, it is a confession. If it denies the claim or asks for discharge without acknowledging the debt, it is not.
5
Note the exceptions
Examples: guarantee for lessor is confession of ownership, but guarantee for lessee is not. Statements like 'so-and-so resides' are confession, but 'he used to reside' are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٢٦
كتاب الإقرار
أمانة قال لي عليك ألف فقال اتزنه أو انتقده أو أجلني به أو قضيتكه أو أحلتك به فهو إقرار وبلا كتابة لا وإن أقر بدين مؤجل وادعى المقر له أنه حال لزمه حالاً وحلف المقر له على الأجل على مائة درهم فهي دراهم مائة وثوب يفسر المائة وكذا مائة وثوبان بخلاف
وجمع بينهما يرجح الدين (لو قال لي عليك ألف فقال اتزنه أو انتقده أو أجلني به أو قضيتكه) أو أعدها أو أرسل غداً من يأخذها يعني يقبضها أو يتزنها أولاً أزنها لك اليوم أو لا تأخذها مني اليوم أو حتى يدخل على مالي أو يقدم على غلامي أو أبرثني عنها أو تصدق علي بها أو وهبها لي مدعياً ذلك أو أحلته بها (فهو إقرار إلا إذا تصادقا أنه على وجه السخرية (وبلا كتابة (لا) كقوله ما قبضت بغير حق جواباً لدعواه أنه قبض منه بغير حق. وقوله أبرئني عن هذه الدعوى أو صالحني عنها، وقوله ما استقرضت من أحد سواك أو غيرك أو قبلك أو بعدك وقضيتك مائة بعد مائة بعد دعوى المائتين بخلاف دفعت إلى أخيك بأمرك وعليه إثبات ذلك وضمانه للآجر ما يجب له على المستأجر إقرار بملك العين للآجر بخلاف ضمانه للمستأجر مال الإجارة في الإجارة الطويلة لا يكون إقراراً بالملك للآجر بخلاف قوله فلان ساكن هذه الدار فإقرار له بها بخلاف كان يسكنها وفلان زرع هذه الأرض أو غرس هذا الكرم أو بنى هذه الدار وهي في يد القائل مدعياً أنه معين أو مستأجر فليس بإقرار بالعين
وكذا هذا الدقيق من طحين فلان بخلاف هذا الطعام من زرع فلان، أو هذا التمر من
نخله أو أرضه أو بستانه أو هذا الصوف من غنمه فهو إقرار كقوله قبضت من أرضه عدل ثياب وشراؤه متنقبة إقرار بالملك للبائع كثوب في جراب وكذا الاستيام والاستيداع والاستعارة والاستيهاب والاستئجار ولو من وكيل وكذا قبول الوديعة. وقوله نعم بعد كلام إقرار مطلقاً، والإيماء بالرأس بعد الاستفهام لا يكون إقراراً بمال وعتق وطلاق وبيع ونكاح وإجارة وهبة بخلاف الكفر والإسلام والنسب والفتوى
426. Book of Confession. Trust: He said to me 'you owe me a thousand', and he said 'weigh it' or 'count it' or 'give me time for it' or 'I paid you' or 'I refer you to someone else for it' – it is a confession. And without writing: no. And if he confessed a deferred debt and the confesse claimed it was due immediately, it is binding immediately, and he makes the confesse swear as to the term. Upon a hundred dirhams, they are dirhams: one hundred and a garment – it explains the hundred; likewise one hundred and two garments – contrary. And between them, he prefers the debt. (If he says to me 'you owe me a thousand', and he says 'weigh it' or 'count it' or 'give me time for it' or 'I paid you' or 'I refer you' or 'I counted them', or 'send someone tomorrow to take them', meaning to take possession or weigh them, or 'first I will weigh them for you today', or 'do not take them from me today', or 'until my property arrives', or 'until my slave comes', or 'release me from them', or 'give charity to me with them', or 'donate them to me' claiming that, or 'I refer you with them' – it is a confession, unless they agree it is in jest. And without writing: no, like his saying 'I did not take possession unjustly' in response to his claim that he took unjustly. And his saying 'discharge me from this claim' or 'settle with me about it', and his saying 'I did not borrow from anyone except you' or 'other than you' or 'before you' or 'after you', and 'I paid you a hundred after a hundred' after a claim of two hundred – contrary to 'I paid your brother by your command' and it is upon him to prove that. And his guarantee for the lessor of what is due to him from the lessee is a confession of ownership of the property for the lessor, contrary to his guarantee for the lessee of the rental payment in a long lease: it is not a confession of ownership for the lessor. Contrary to his saying 'so-and-so is a resident of this house' – it is a confession of it for him; contrary to 'he used to reside in it'. And 'so-and-so cultivated this land' or 'planted this vine' or 'built this house' while it is in the hand of the speaker claiming that he is a tenant or lessee – it is not a confession of the property. Likewise, 'this flour from so-and-so's grinding' – contrary to 'this food from so-and-so's crop', or 'this dates from his palm tree' or 'his land' or 'his garden', or 'this wool from his sheep' – it is a confession, like his saying 'I received from his land a load of garments' and 'his purchase of a woman wearing a face-veil' is a confession of ownership for the seller like a garment in a bag. Likewise, requesting a price, depositing, borrowing, requesting charity, hiring even from an agent, and likewise accepting a deposit. And his saying 'yes' after speech is an absolute confession. And nodding the head after a question is not a confession of property, emancipation, divorce, sale, marriage, hire, or gift – contrary to unbelief, Islam, lineage, and legal opinion.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
هذا الجزء من البحر الرائق يوضح الألفاظ التي تعتبر إقراراً بالدين والتي لا تعتبر. يبدأ بقوله: إذا قال له شخص 'لك علي ألف' فرد المدين بقوله 'اتزنه' أو 'انتقده' أو 'أجلني به' أو 'قضيتكه' أو 'أحلتك به'، فكل هذه الأجوبة تعتبر إقراراً بالدين. أما إذا قال 'احملها' أو 'أرسل غداً من يأخذها' فكذلك. ويستثنى ما إذا كان الكلام على وجه السخرية متفقاً عليه. ثم يذكر أن بعض الأجوبة لا تعتبر إقراراً، مثل قوله 'ما قبضت بغير حق' رداً على دعوى القبض بغير حق، وقوله 'أبرئني' أو 'صالحني'، وقوله 'ما استقرضت من أحد سواك' ونحو ذلك. ثم يفرق بين ضمان المؤجر (يعتبر إقراراً بملك العين للمؤجر) وضمان المستأجر (لا يعتبر إقراراً في الإجارة الطويلة). ويبين أن وصف شخص بأنه 'ساكن' الدار إقرار له بالملك، بخلاف 'كان يسكنها'. وأخيراً يذكر أن الإشارة بالرأس بعد الاستفهام لا تعتبر إقراراً في المعاملات المالية والأحوال الشخصية إلا في الكفر والإسلام والنسب والفتوى.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): اعتراف الشخص بحق عليه للغير، وهو ملزم إذا صدر بصريح اللفظ أو بما يقوم مقامه.
الإيماء بالرأس (al-īmā' bi al-ra's): الإشارة بالرأس بعد سؤال لا تعتبر إقراراً في معظم الأحكام المالية والمدنية عند الحنفية.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT considered a confession of debt?
A) 'Weigh it'
B) 'Give me time'
C) 'I did not take it unjustly'
D) 'I paid you'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a verbal response to a debt claim is a confession only if it directly or indirectly acknowledges the debt, not if it denies or raises a defense.

Non-Verbal Indications: Nodding and Its Legal Effect
Ruling on nodding as a confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when nodding the head constitutes a confession and when it does not in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A nod is a confession for faith and lineage, but not for property or transactions.

Non-verbal communication can sometimes create legal obligations. In Hanafi fiqh, nodding the head after a question has different effects depending on the subject matter. This lesson focuses on the specific rule that nodding is not a valid confession for financial matters, divorces, sales, etc., but it is valid for matters of faith, Islam, lineage, and legal opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
The rule applies after a question (istifham) is posed to someone. The person nods in response.
2
Determine the subject matter
Hanafi law divides matters into two categories: property/transactions (mal, itq, talaq, bay', nikah, ijara, hibah) and personal status/religion (kufr, islam, nasab, fatwa).
3
Apply the rule for property/transactions
For property, emancipation, divorce, sale, marriage, hire, and gift, nodding is NOT a confession. The person's silence or nod does not create liability or change status.
4
Apply the rule for personal status/religion
For matters of unbelief, Islam, lineage, and legal opinion, nodding IS a confession. This is an exception (bikhilaf).
5
Note the rationale
The distinction likely stems from the seriousness of the matters: financial and marital rights require explicit verbal clarity, while matters of faith and lineage can be established by unambiguous non-verbal cues in certain contexts.

Confession of Deferred Debt and Ambiguous Numbers with Weights/Measures
Rulings on iqrar (confession) and interpretation of numerical expressions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a confessed deferred debt is claimed to be due immediately, and interpret ambiguous numbers when conjuncted with weighed or measured items.

Core Idea
An ambiguous number is clarified by a conjuncted weighed or measured item, turning '100 and a dirham' into 101 dirhams.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq covers two interconnected issues: the binding nature of a deferred debt confession when the creditor claims it is due, and the rule for interpreting numbers like 'one hundred and a dirham'. Understanding these rules is crucial for correctly determining obligations in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main issues
The passage first addresses the ruling when a debtor confesses a deferred debt but the creditor claims it is due immediately. Then it turns to the interpretation of ambiguous numbers when conjuncted with a weighed or measured item.
2
Analyze the deferred debt confession rule
If the debtor admits a deferred debt but the creditor denies the deferment, the debt becomes immediately binding on the debtor. The creditor is also made to swear that it is due.
Contrast with black dirhams: if he confesses black dirhams and denies their description, it is still binding.
3
Understand the ambiguous number rule
If someone confesses an ambiguous number (e.g., 'one hundred') and conjuncts a weighed or measured item (e.g., 'and a dirham'), the item clarifies the number: 'one hundred and a dirham' means 101 dirhams.
This applies only to weighed/measured items (mithliyyat), not to qimiyyat (valuables like a garment).
4
Apply the linguistic rule about waw in compound numbers
The passage notes that in numbers like 'eleven thousand', the waw should be dropped: it is 'twenty-one thousand', not 'twenty and one thousand'. This is a standard Arabic rule.
The rule is qiyasi (analogical) and applies wherever possible.
5
Note the exception for qimi items
If the conjuncted item is a qimi (e.g., a garment), it does not clarify the number but adds a separate item: 'one hundred and a garment' means 100 dirhams and a garment, not 101 garments.
The distinction is based on whether the item is mithli (fungible) or qimi (non-fungible).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقر بدين مؤجل وادعى المقر له أنه حال لزمه حالاً كإقراره بعبد في يده أنه لرجل وأنه استأجره منه (ويستحلف المقر له فيهما) بخلاف ما لو أقر بالدراهم السود فكذبه في صفتها يلزمه أما أقر به فقط كإقرار الكفيل بدين مؤجل ولمن عليه دين مؤجل إذا خاف لو اعترف به لا يصدقه إنكار أصل الدين إذا لم يرد توى حقه ومن أقر بعدد مبهم وعطف موزوناً أو مكيلاً كان بياناً له (كمائة ودرهم) أو درهمان أو ثلاثة دراهم فهي دراهم) عطف عليه قيمياً واحداً (لا كمائة وثوب) أو وثوبان وإن متعدداً فبيان (كمائة وثلاثة أثواب ولو قال نصف درهم ودينار وثوب فعليه نصف كل
أحد عشر
ألفاً فيلزم أن تهدر الواو التي تعتبر مهما أمكن وهنا ممكن فيقال أحد وعشرون ألفاً ومائة وأحد وعشرون درهماً. نعم قوله ولو سدس «الخ) مستقيم أي فيقال فيه مائة ألف وأحد وعشرون ألفاً ومائة وأحد وعشرون درهماً لا أنه مستقيم زيادة على العشرة الآلاف
And if he confessed a deferred debt and the confesse claimed that it was due immediately, it is binding immediately, like his confession of a slave in his hand that he is a man's and that he hired him from him (and the confesse is made to swear in both cases). Contrary to if he confessed black dirhams and he denied their description – it is binding upon him. But if he confessed it only, like the confession of a guarantor of a deferred debt, and for the one who owes a deferred debt, if he fears that if he admits it, his denial of the origin of the debt will not be believed if he does not intend to harm his right. And whoever confessed an ambiguous number and conjuncted it with a weighed or measured item, it is an explanation for it (like one hundred and a dirham) or two dirhams or three dirhams – they are dirhams conjuncted to it as one valuable item, not (like one hundred and a garment) or two garments, and if multiple, it is an explanation (like one hundred and three garments). And if he said 'half a dirham, a dinar, and a garment', he owes half of each. Eleven thousand: it is necessary that the waw which is considered wherever possible is dropped, and here it is possible, so it is said 'twenty-one thousand and one hundred and twenty-one dirhams'. Yes, his saying 'and if a sixth' etc. is correct, i.e. it is said therein 'one hundred thousand and twenty-one thousand and one hundred and twenty-one dirhams', but it does not correct the increase beyond the ten thousand.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
هذا المقطع يتناول عدة مسائل: أولاً: إذا أقر بدين مؤجل لكن المقر له ادعى أنه حال، فإنه يلزمه حالاً ويحلف المقر له على التأجيل. ثانياً: مسألة الإقرار بالدراهم السوداء (المغشوشة) وتكذيب الصفة – يلزمه بها. ثالثاً: قاعدة تفسير العدد المبهم إذا عطف عليه موزون أو مكيل: فالعطف يبين العدد، مثلاً 'مائة ودرهم' تعني مائة درهم ودرهماً واحداً أي 101 درهم. أما إذا عطف عليه قيمي كالثوب، فإنه لا يبين العدد بل يكون شيئاً آخر، مثل 'مائة وثوب' تعني مائة درهم وثوباً. ثم يبين قاعدة لغوية: إذا قال 'أحد عشر ألفاً' وجب حذف الواو في العطف لتصبح 'أحد وعشرون ألفاً' وهكذا. وينتهي بتصحيح قول من قال إن 'سدس' يزيد على عشرة آلاف، بل الصواب أنه يقال 'مائة ألف وأحد وعشرون ألفاً ومائة وأحد وعشرون درهماً'.

Key Terms
عدد مبهم (ʻadad mubham): العدد الذي لم يحدد بقدر معين، كأن يقول 'مائة' دون تمييز، فيحتاج إلى بيان.
الواو (al-wāw): حرف العطف الذي يعتبر مهما أمكن، لكنه قد يسقط في تركيب الأعداد كقول 'أحد وعشرون' بدون واو بعد 'أحد'.
موزون (mawzūn): المكيل أو الموزون من المثليات التي يمكن الاتحاد في أفرادها.
قيمي (qīmī): ما ليس بمثلي، كالثوب، فلا يبين العدد المبهم.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
إذا قال شخص 'له علي مائة ودرهم'، كم يلزمه؟
أ) مائة درهم
ب) مائة درهم ودرهم واحد (101)
ج) مائة وواحد درهم
د) درهم واحد

Key Takeaway
An ambiguous number is explained by a conjuncted weighed/measured item, and a deferred debt becomes immediately binding if the creditor denies the deferment.

Acknowledgment of Debt from Unreceived Sale Price
Conditional rulings on iqrar for unpaid sale price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on acknowledging a debt from an unreceived sale price when the sold item is specified or unspecified, and identify when the acknowledgment is binding.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment of debt from an unpaid sale price is binding if the item is unspecified; if specified, binding depends on confirmation.

In Hanafi fiqh, an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt arising from a sale where the price was not received is treated differently based on whether the sold item is identified (mu'ayyan) or not. This lesson will clarify the conditions under which the acknowledger is liable, including scenarios of confirmation and denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial statement
Examine the scenario: someone says 'I owe a thousand from the price of a slave which I have not received.' The ruling depends on whether the slave is specified (mu'ayyan) or not.
The slave being mu'ayyan means it is a particular identifiable slave.
2
Apply the ruling for a specified slave
If the slave is specified, the acknowledgee (buyer) must confirm the sale and hand over the slave. If he confirms and hands over, the debt is binding. If he denies the slave is his, no debt is due. If he confirms the slave is the acknowledger's but claims a different sale, mutual oaths (tahaluf) determine possession.
Al-Zayla'i expands: when both agree on the slave but differ on the cause, the acknowledgment stands.
3
Apply the ruling for an unspecified slave
If the slave is not specified (e.g., not identified), the thousand is binding absolutely, and the acknowledger's claim of non-receipt is not accepted.
This is similar to acknowledging a debt for prohibited items like wine.
4
Consider the expansion from commentary
Al-Zayla'i explains the second aspect: if the acknowledgee says 'the slave is your slave, I bought another' – the ruling is the same as the first because they agree on the underlying right.
The difference in cause does not affect the binding nature of the acknowledgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال على ألف من ثمن عبد لم أقبضه فإن كان العبد معيناً فإما أن يصدقه ويسلمه أولاً، فإن صدقه وسلمه لزمه ألف، وكذا إن صدقه على بيع عبد غيره فإن المعين ملك المقر، سواء كان في يده أو في يد المقر له كإقراره بألف غصباً فقال هي قرض، وإن لم يصدقه على العبد لا يلزمه شيء وإن صدقه على أن المبيع غيره وأن المعين ليس ملك المقر بتحالفات بيع ويسقط المال والعبد لمن هو في يده، وإن لم يكن العبد معيناً لزمه الألف مطلقاً ولا يقبل قوله إن لم يقبضه كقوله من ثمن خمر أو خنزير أو مال القمار أو حر أو ميتة أو دم قوله : (فإن كان العبد معيناً الخ) قال الزيلعي : هذه المسألة على وجوه أحدها ما ذكره المصنف وهو ما إذا صدقه وسلمه إليه وحكمه ما ذكره لأن ما ثبت بتصادقهما يكون كالثابت عياناً. والثاني أن يقول المقر له العبد عبدك ما بعتكه وإنما بعتك عبداً آخر وسلمته إليك والحكم فيه كالأول لأنهما اتفقا على ما أقر به من أن كل واحد منهما يستحق ما أقر به غير أنهما اختلفا في سبب الاستحقاق، ولا يبالي باختلافهما ولا باختلاف السبب عند حصول يصح
And if he says: 'I owe a thousand from the price of a slave which I have not received', then if the slave is specified, either he confirms him and hands him over first: if he confirms him and hands him over, a thousand is binding. Similarly, if he confirms the sale of another slave, then the specified [slave] is the property of the acknowledger, whether it is in his hand or in the hand of the acknowledgee, like his acknowledgment of a thousand as a usurpation and he says it is a loan. If he does not confirm the slave, nothing is binding. If he confirms that the sold item is another and that the specified slave is not the property of the acknowledger, with mutual oaths of sale, the money and the slave go to the one in whose hand it is. If the slave is not specified, the thousand is binding absolutely, and his statement 'I have not received it' is not accepted, like his saying 'from the price of wine or pork or gambling money or a free person or a corpse or blood'. His saying: (If the slave is specified, etc.) al-Zayla'i said: This issue has several aspects. One is what the author mentioned, which is when he confirms him and hands him over to him, and its ruling is as he mentioned because what is established by their mutual confirmation is like what is established by sight. The second is that the acknowledgee says: 'The slave is your slave, I did not buy him from you, but I bought another slave from you and handed him over to you' — the ruling is like the first because they agree on what he acknowledged, that each of them is entitled to what he acknowledged, except they differ on the cause of entitlement, and no attention is paid to their difference nor to the difference in cause when it occurs.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: someone acknowledges a debt of one thousand dirhams as the price of a slave that he sold but did not receive the payment. The ruling depends on whether the slave is specified (mu'ayyan) or not. If the slave is specified, the acknowledgee (the buyer) must confirm the sale and hand over the slave. If he does, the debt is binding on the acknowledger (the seller). If the acknowledgee claims the slave is not the one sold but another, and they agree on the slave being the seller's property, the debt is still binding because they agree on the underlying right. If the acknowledgee denies the slave altogether, no debt is due. If the acknowledgee claims the slave was sold to him by another person, the case goes to mutual oaths (tahaluf) and the property goes to the one in possession. If the slave is not specified, the acknowledger is liable for the thousand absolutely, and his excuse of non-receipt is not accepted, similar to acknowledgment for illegal items like wine. Al-Zayla'i's commentary clarifies two scenarios: the first is the straightforward case; the second is when the acknowledgee confirms the slave is the seller's but says he bought another slave. This is still valid because the acknowledgment of the debt is based on the agreed fact.

Key Terms
ثمن عبد (thaman ʿabd): Price of a slave, i.e., a debt arising from a sale of a slave.
معين (muʿayyan): Specified, identified individually.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or admission of a right or debt.
تصادق (tasāduq): Mutual confirmation or agreement between parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe 1000 dirhams from the price of a slave I have not received' and the slave is not specified, what is the ruling?
A) The debt is not binding because the slave is not received.
B) The debt is binding unless he proves non-receipt.
C) The debt is binding and his excuse is not accepted.
D) The debt is binding only if the acknowledgee confirms.

Key Takeaway
An acknowledgment of debt from an unpaid sale price is binding if the item is unspecified; if specified, it is binding only if the acknowledgee confirms the sale and hands over the item.

Sulh on Destroyed Usurped Property: Validity Before and After Judgment
Ruling with analogy on timing of sulh validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sulh for more than market value is valid before court valuation but invalid after, and identify the analogous case of joint slave emancipation.

Core Idea
Sulh for more than value is valid before judgment — after judgment, it is invalid and binds no one.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical timing condition in Hanafi contract law: when can a settlement for more than actual value be enforced? The ruling distinguishes between voluntary negotiation and post-judgment settlement, with significant consequences for the parties. Understanding this distinction prevents disputes over liability and ensures that court-determined obligations remain intact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two situations: (1) settlement before court valuation, (2) settlement after court valuation. Also an analogous case of joint slave emancipation.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1: permissible (valid). For scenario 2: impermissible (invalid). The same rule applies to the emancipation analogy.
The hukm level is sahih (valid) for the first and batil (invalid) for the second.
3
Understand the legal effect of timing
After judgment, the settlement is batil; the parties revert to the court-determined value. The usurper cannot later claim a lower value to reduce payment, even if both agree.
The post-judgment period fixes liability; any extra payment lacks consideration.
4
Apply the analogy to joint emancipation
If a solvent partner frees a jointly owned slave, then settles with the other partner for half the value after judgment, it is invalid, just like the first case after valuation.
The illa (effective cause) is that the valuation has already been determined by the court.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلح عن المغصوب الهالك على أكثر من قيمته قبل القضاء بالقيمة جائز، فلا تقبل بينة الغاصب بعده على أن قيمته أقل مما صالح عليه ولا رجوع للغاصب لو تصادقا بعده على أنها أقل ولو أعتق موسر عبداً مشتركاً فصالح الشريك على نصف قيمته لا يجوز كالصلح في الأول بعد القضاء بالقيمة.
And settlement regarding the destroyed usurped property for more than its value before judgment of value is permissible. So the testimony of the usurper afterwards that its value is less than what he settled for is not accepted, and the usurper has no recourse if they both agree afterwards that it was less. And if a solvent man emancipates a jointly owned slave and then the partner settles for half its value, it is not permissible, like the settlement in the first case after judgment of value.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage states rulings on sulh (compromise) for usurped property that has been destroyed. The Hanafi position: It is permissible to settle for more than the market value before a judge has determined the value. After the judgment, such a settlement is not valid. The usurper cannot later claim that the actual value was lower; even if both parties agree, the settlement stands. The second part draws an analogy to a jointly owned slave: if a solvent partner emancipates the slave and the other partner settles for half the value after judgment, it is invalid, similar to the first case.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise or settlement between parties to avoid litigation, often involving partial payment or exchange.
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation, wrongful taking of another's property without consent.
قيمة (qīmah): The market value or assessed value of property at the time of judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to settle for more than the value of destroyed usurped property?
A) After the court judgment
B) Before the court judgment
C) Never
D) Only if both parties agree after judgment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, sulh for more than market value is only valid before court valuation; after judgment it is invalid, preserving the court's determination of liability.

Deferment of Compensation for Usurped Property
Rulings on deferring compensation for usurped property absent or extant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which deferment of compensation for usurped property is valid or void, and apply the ruling to cases of absent and extant property.

Core Idea
Deferment is valid only if the property is extant or, if absent, is a described measured/weighed item.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on deferring compensation (badal) for usurped property (maghsūb) in a sulh settlement. The key distinction is whether the property is still present or has absconded (ābiq), and whether it is determinate (mut'ayyan) or non-determinate. Understanding these conditions is crucial for valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is deferment of compensation in a sulh for usurped property. The ruling varies: it is sahih (valid) under certain conditions, and fasid (void) otherwise.
2
Distinguish between absent and extant property
For absent property (ābīq), deferment of compensation is generally invalid unless the property is described and measured/weighed. For extant property, deferment is always permissible and the transaction is a sale.
3
Understand the concept of ta'ayyun
Non-determinate property (like debts) is not tied to a specific object; deferment of its compensation is fasid unless it is described and measured/weighed. Determinate property (ayn) is not invalidated by separation before receipt.
4
Apply the dispute scenario
When the usurper claims the property did not abscond, his statement is accepted, and a sulh on deferred food is valid, analogous to buying a slave with a condition of freedom.
5
Summarize the operative ruling
The mufta bihi is that deferment is valid for extant property and for absent described measured/weighed items; otherwise it is fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تأجيل بدل المغصوب المصالح عليه بعد إباقه إذا كان مما لا يتعين إلا إذا كان مكيلاً أو موزوناً موصوفاً مؤجلاً فهو فاسد كما لو لم يكن مؤجلاً وفارقه قبل التعيين، وإن كان بعينه لم يبطل بالافتراق قبل القبض. وإن كان المصالح عنه المغصوب قائماً جاز تأجيل بدله مطلقاً وكان بيعاً. ولو ادعى الغاصب عدم إباقه وأنه في بيته والمولى إباقه ثم صالحه على طعام مؤجل جاز عملاً بقول الغاصب لكون العوض مستحقاً عليه ولدعواه الصحة كشرائه عبداً بحريته نظراً إلى زعم البائع وقبول قوله في مقداره
Deferment of the compensation for the usurped property that is the subject of settlement after it has absconded if it is of a type that is not determinate, except if it is a measured or weighed item described with a deferred term, then it is void, just as if it were not deferred and they separated before specification. And if it is determinate (ayn), it is not invalidated by separation before receipt. And if the usurped property that is the subject of settlement is still extant, deferment of its compensation is absolutely permissible and it is a sale. And if the usurper claims that it did not abscond and that it is in his house, but the owner claims it absconded, and then he settles with him on deferred food, it is permissible, acting on the statement of the usurper because the compensation is due from him and because of his claim of validity, like purchasing a slave with the condition of his freedom, considering the claim of the seller and accepting his statement regarding its amount.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage discusses deferment (ta'jīl) of compensation in sulh for usurped property. If the property is absent (ābīq) and non-determinate (e.g., a debt), deferment is void unless the property is measured or weighed and described with a future term. If it is determinate (ayn), separation before receipt does not invalidate. If the property is still extant, deferment is valid and the transaction is a sale. In a dispute over whether the property absconded, the usurper's statement is accepted, and sulh on deferred food is valid, analogous to buying a slave with a condition of freedom.

Key Terms
إباق (ibāq): Absconding, i.e., the property is missing or its location unknown.
تعين (ta'ayyun): Becoming determinate or specified; non-determinate property is like debts not tied to a specific object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is deferment of compensation for absent property valid according to the passage?
A) Always
B) Only if the property is non-determinate
C) If the compensation is a described measured or weighed item with a deferred term
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Deferment of compensation for usurped property is valid unconditionally for extant property and for absent property described and measured/weighed; otherwise it is fasid.

Sulh in Debt: Taking Part and Dropping the Remainder
Defining sulh in debt as taking part and dropping remainder, not a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sulh in debt under Hanafi law and distinguish it from a sale by applying the rule that it is a partial waiver, not an exchange.

Core Idea
Sulh in debt is not a sale; it is taking part and dropping the rest.

Settlement of debts (sulh) is a common way to resolve disputes without litigation. The Hanafi school clarifies a key point: when the settlement is on the same type of debt, it is NOT a sale (bay') but rather a release (ibra') of part of the claim. This distinction affects validity and other rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the Arabic definition: 'أخذ لبعض حقه وإسقاط للباقي' (taking part of his right and dropping the remainder). Understand that the creditor takes a portion and waives the rest.
2
Classify the legal nature
The author explicitly says it is not a transaction (mu'awada) but a waiver. This is key to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine the examples
The source gives several examples: settling 1000 for 500, or for deferred payment, or for different quality coins. Identify what remains constant: the settlement is on the same type of right.
The condition of same type (jins) is implicit.
4
Apply the definition
Given a scenario, state whether it is sulh in debt (valid as waiver) or a sale (needs different rules).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلح في الدين اه وكل شيء وقع عليه (الصلح) وهو من جنس ما يستحقه المدعي على المدعى عليه (بعقد المداينة) أي البيع بالدين لم يحمل على المعاوضة وإنما هو (أخذ لبعض حقه وإسقاط للباقي فلو صالح عن ألف على نصفه أو على ألف مؤجل أو خمسمائة مؤجلة أو جياد على خمسمائة زيوف حالة أو مؤجلة أو عن ألف مؤجلة على ألف حالة مقبوضة أو عن عن ألف
Chapter of Settlement in Debt. And everything upon which settlement occurs, and it is of the same type as what the claimant is entitled to from the defendant by a contract of debt, i.e., sale on credit, it is not considered a transaction; rather it is taking some of his right and dropping the remainder. So if he settles for one thousand for half of it, or for one thousand deferred, or five hundred deferred, or good [coins] for five hundred counterfeit coins immediate or deferred, or for one thousand deferred for one thousand immediate received, or for one thousand for...
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is the opening of the chapter on sulh in debt (الصلح في الدين). The author defines that when the settlement is on the same type of debt (e.g., one thousand on a debt of one thousand), it is not considered a contract of exchange (mu'āwaḍah) but rather taking part and waiving the rest. Several examples are given: settling one thousand for half (500), or for a deferred thousand, or for 500 deferred, or for good coins in place of counterfeit, etc. The ruling is that such sulh is valid as a release of rights, not a sale.

Key Terms
الصلح في الدين (al-ṣulḥ fī al-dayn): Settlement between a creditor and debtor where the creditor takes part of what is due and forgives the remainder.
مداينة (mudāyanah): A debt contract, typically a sale on credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, sulh in debt is characterized as:
A) A sale of debt
B) A gift of the entire debt
C) Taking part of the right and dropping the remainder
D) A loan repayment

Key Takeaway
Sulh in debt is taking part and dropping the rest, not a sale.
